A [[federal parliamentary republic]] state, Pakistan is a federation that comprises [[Four Provinces (Pakistan)|four provinces]]: [[Punjab, Pakistan|Punjab]], [[Khyber Pakhtunkhwa|Khyber-Pakhtunkhwa]], [[Sindh]], and [[Balochistan, Pakistan|Balochistan]].&lt;ref&gt;Article 1(1)â€“2(d) of the [http://pakistani.org/pakistan/constitution/part1.html Part I: Introductory] in the [[Constitution of Pakistan]]&lt;/ref&gt; and four [[Administrative units of Pakistan|territories]]: the [[Federally Administered Tribal Areas|Tribal belt]], [[Gilgitâ€“Baltistan]], [[Islamabad Capital Territory]], and [[Azad Kashmir|Kashmir]]. The [[Government of Pakistan]] exercises the [[De facto standard|''de facto'']] jurisdiction over the [[Frontier Regions]] and the [[Western Kashmir|western parts]] of the [[Kashmir Region]]s, which are organised into the separate political entities [[Azad Kashmir]] and [[Gilgitâ€“Baltistan]] (formerly Northern Areas). In 2009, the [[Constitution of Pakistan|constitutional assignment]] ({{small|the ''Gilgitâ€“Baltistan Empowerment and Self-Governance Order''}}) awarded the [[Gilgitâ€“Baltistan]] a [[Provinces of Pakistan|semi-provincial status]], giving it self-government.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite journal|url=http://www.pid.gov.pk/Prime%20Minister.doc|publisher=Press Information Department, Pakistan|format=DOC|title=Highlights of Prime Minister's Press Talk on &quot;Gilgitâ€“Baltistan Empowerment and Self Governance Order âˆ’2009&quot; at PM'S Secretariat on August 29, 2009|year=2009|accessdate=29 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The [[Local government in Pakistan|local government]] system consists of a three-tier system of [[Districts of pakistan|districts]], [[tehsil]]s and [[Union Councils of Pakistan|union councils]], with an elected body at each tier.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=Decentralization in Pakistan|url=http://www.worldbank.org.pk/WBSITE/EXTERNAL/COUNTRIES/SOUTHASIAEXT/PAKISTANEXTN/0,,contentMDK:21973776~pagePK:141137~piPK:141127~theSitePK:293052,00.html|publisher=World Bank|accessdate=29 December 2011|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20100130094603/http://www.worldbank.org.pk:80/WBSITE/EXTERNAL/COUNTRIES/SOUTHASIAEXT/PAKISTANEXTN/0,,contentMDK:21973776~pagePK:141137~piPK:141127~theSitePK:293052,00.html|archivedate=30 January 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; There are about 130 districts altogether, of which Azad Kashmir has ten&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=Azad Jammu and Kashmir Districts|url=http://www.ajk.gov.pk/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=42&amp;Itemid=12|publisher=Government of AJK|accessdate=29 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; and Gilgitâ€“Baltistan seven.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite journal|url=http://www.dunyanews.tv/newsite/other/GilgitBaltistan.pdf|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20100919114343/http://dunyanews.tv/newsite/other/GilgitBaltistan.pdf|archivedate=19 September 2010|publisher=Dunya|format=PDF|title=Gilgitâ€“Baltistan Empowerment and Self Governance Order|year=2009|page=1}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Tribal Areas comprise seven tribal agencies and six small frontier regions detached from neighbouring districts.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=Map of Agencies and Regions in the FATA|url=http://fata.gov.pk/images/stories/fata1.png|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130928161600/http://fata.gov.pk/images/stories/fata1.png|archivedate=28 September 2013|work=fata.gov.pk|format=PNG|accessdate=29 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;

{{Pakistan Administrative Units Image Map}}

[[Law enforcement in Pakistan|Law enforcement]] is carried out by a joint network of the [[Pakistan Intelligence Community|intelligence community]] with jurisdiction limited to the relevant province or territory. The [[National Intelligence Directorate]] coordinates the information intelligence at both federal and provincial level; including the [[Federal Investigation Agency|FIA]], [[Intelligence Bureau (Pakistan)|IB]], [[National Highways and Motorway Police|Motorway Police]], and [[Paramilitary forces of Pakistan|paramilitary forces]] such as the [[Pakistan Rangers]] and the [[Frontier Corps]].&lt;ref name=&quot;law&quot;&gt;{{cite book|author=Asad Jamal|title=Police Organisations in Pakistan|year=2010|publisher=CHRI and HRCP|isbn=81-88205-79-6|pages=9â€“15}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pakistan's &quot;premier&quot; intelligence agency, the Inter-Services Intelligene (ISI), was formed just within a year after the Independence of Pakistan in 1947.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book|author=Manoj Shrivastava|title=Re-Energising Indian Intelligence|publisher=Vij Books India Pvt Ltd|date=1 April 2013|isbn=9789382573555|page=89}}&lt;/ref&gt; Inter Service Intelligence Agency of Pakistan was ranked as the top intelligence agency in the world in 2011, 2014 and 2015.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/intelligence-agencies-world-2011-261075|title=Top Intelligence Agencies of the World|author=Aditya Rangroo|work=International Business Times UK|accessdate=20 February 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.pakistantribe.com/top-news/47229/heres-why-isi-ranked-top-best-intelligence-agency-in-the-world|title=Here's Why ISI Ranked Top Best Intelligence Agency Of The World â€“ Pakistan Tribe|author=Web Desk|work=Pakistan Tribe|accessdate=20 February 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The [[court system of Pakistan|court system]] is organised as a hierarchy, with the [[Supreme Court of Pakistan|Supreme Court]] at the apex, below which are [[High Courts of Pakistan|High Courts]], [[Federal Shariat Court]]s (one in each province and one in the federal capital), [[District Courts of Pakistan|District Courts]] (one in each district), Judicial Magistrate Courts (in every town and city), Executive Magistrate Courts and civil courts. The [[Pakistan penal code|Penal code]] has limited jurisdiction in the Tribal Areas, where law is largely derived from tribal customs.&lt;ref name=&quot;law&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|author=Faqir Hussain|title=The Judicial System Of Pakistan|url=http://www.supremecourt.gov.pk/web/user_files/File/thejudicialsystemofPakistan.pdf|work=Supreme Court of Pakistan|format=PDF|year=2009|pages=10â€“21|accessdate=26 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Military===
{{Main article|Pakistan Armed Forces}}
&lt;!--THIS SECTION IS A SUMMARYâ€”PLEASE ADD NEW MATERIAL TO THE MAIN ARTICLE--&gt;
[[File:F-16 Red Flag 2010 Pakistan Air Force 9 sqn Griffins.jpg|thumb|right|The [[Pakistan Air Force]] [[General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon|F16s]] in tight formation in [[Nevada]], U.S during a joint US-Pakistan air force exercise.]]

The armed forces of Pakistan are the [[List of countries by number of troops|eighth largest]] in the world in terms of numbers in full-time service, with about 617,000 personnel on active duty and 513,000 reservists, as of tentative estimates in 2010.&lt;ref name=&quot;Hackett&quot;&gt;{{cite book|title=The Military Balance 2010|author1=International Institute for Strategic Studies|author2=Hackett, James (ed.)|year=2010|publisher=[[Routledge]]|location=London|isbn=1-85743-557-5|pages=367â€“370}}&lt;/ref&gt; They [[Military history of Pakistan|came into existence]] after independence in 1947, and the [[Pakistani military establishment|military establishment]] has frequently influenced in the [[Politics of Pakistan|national politics]] ever since.&lt;ref name=&quot;military&quot; /&gt; [[Chain of command]] of the military is kept under the control of the [[Joint Chiefs of Staff Committee]]; all of the branches joint works, coordination, military logistics, and joint missions are under the [[Joint Staff Headquarters (Pakistan)|Joint Staff HQ]].&lt;ref name=&quot;Diane Publishing Co.&quot;&gt;{{cite book|last1=Blood|first1=Peter R.|title=Pakistan|date=1995|publisher=Diane Publishing Co.|location=Washington D.C.|isbn=0788136313|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=DRMTO7mn7hIC&amp;pg=PA287&amp;dq=joint+chiefs+of+staff+committee&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=KhGAVN79GNjjoASW3oCoCg&amp;ved=0CFkQuwUwCA#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=true|accessdate=4 December 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt; The [[Joint Staff Headquarters (Pakistan)|Joint Staff HQ]] is composed of the [[AHQ (PAF)|Air HQ]], [[NHQ (PN)|Navy HQ]], and [[General Headquarters (Pakistan Army)|Army GHQ]] in the vicinity of the [[Rawalpindi Cantonment|Rawalpindi Military District]].&lt;ref name=&quot;Frankfort, IL&quot;&gt;{{cite book|last=Singh|first=R.S.N.|title=The military factor in Pakistan|year=2008|publisher=Frankfort, IL|location=New Delhi|isbn=0981537898|url=https://books.google.com/?id=wCm2DFZblOYC&amp;pg=PA409&amp;dq=joint+chiefs+of+staff+committee+pakistan#v=onepage&amp;q=joint%20chiefs%20of%20staff%20committee%20pakistan&amp;f=true}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The [[Chairman Joint Chiefs of Staff Committee]] is the highest [[Staff Officer|principle staff officer]] in the armed forces, and the chief military adviser to the [[GoP|civilian government]] though the chairman has no authority over the three branches of armed forces.&lt;ref name=&quot;Diane Publishing Co.&quot; /&gt; The [[Chairman Joint Chiefs of Staff Committee|Chairman joint chiefs]] controls the military from the [[Joint Staff Headquarters (Pakistan)|JS HQ]] and maintains strategic communications between the military and the civilian government.&lt;ref name=&quot;Diane Publishing Co.&quot; /&gt; As of current, the [[Chairman Joint Chiefs of Staff Committee|Chairman joint chiefs]] is General [[Rashad Mahmood|Rashid Mahmood]] alongside [[Chief of Army Staff (Pakistan)|chief of army staff]] General [[Raheel Sharif]],&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|author=Mateen Haider|url=http://dawn.com/news/1058927/raheel-sharif-being-appointed-new-army-chief|newspaper=Dawn|title=Lt Gen Raheel Sharif chosen as new army chief|publisher=Dawn.Com|date=27 November 2013|accessdate=28 November 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; [[Chief of Naval Staff (Pakistan)|chief of naval staff]] [[Admiral]] [[Muhammad Zakaullah|Muhammad Zaka]],&lt;ref name=&quot;ISPR (Navy Division)&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Chief of Naval Staff|url=http://www.paknavy.gov.pk/cns.html|website=http://www.paknavy.gov.pk/|publisher=ISPR (Navy Division)|accessdate=3 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; and [[Chief of Air Staff (Pakistan)|chief of air staff]] [[Air Chief Marshal]] [[Suhail Aman]].&lt;ref name=&quot;ISPR (Air Force)&quot;&gt;{{cite web|last1=OAF|title=Chief of Air Staff|url=http://www.paf.gov.pk/cas_intro.html|website=http://www.paf.gov.pk/|publisher=ISPR (Air Force)|accessdate=26 April 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; The main branches are the [[Pakistan Army|Army]]â€“[[PAF|Air Force]]â€“[[Pakistan Navy|Navy]]â€“[[Pakistan Marines|Marines]], which are supported by the number of [[Paramilitary forces of Pakistan|paramilitary forces]] in the country.&lt;ref name=&quot;china22&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Pakistan Armed Forces|url=http://www.cdi.org/issues/Asia/PAKISTAN.html|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/19980210034847/http://www.cdi.org/issues/Asia/PAKISTAN.html|archivedate=10 February 1998|publisher=Center For Defense Information|accessdate=24 July 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; Control over the [[Pakistan's nuclear testing series|strategic arsenals]], deployment, employment, development, [[Command, Control, Communications, Computers, Intelligence, Surveillance, and Reconnaissance|military computers]] and [[Nuclear command and control|command and control]] is a responsibility vested under the [[National Command Authority (Pakistan)|National Command Authority]] which oversaw the work on the [[Nuclear Doctrine of Pakistan|nuclear policy]] as part of the credible [[N-deterrence|minimum deterrence]].&lt;ref name=&quot;Stanford University Press&quot; /&gt;

The [[United States]], [[Turkey]], and [[Peoples Republic of China|China]] maintain close military relations and regularly export military equipment and [[technology transfer]] to Pakistan.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://armstrade.sipri.org/armstrade/page/values.php|title=Importer/Exporter TIV Tables|publisher=Armstrade.sipri.org|accessdate=16 April 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; Joint logistics and major [[Military exercise|war games]] are occasionally carried out by the militaries of [[Peoples Republic of China|China]] and [[Turkey]].&lt;ref name=&quot;china22&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Pakistan and China participate in drill|url=http://www.dawn.com/2011/11/26/pak-china-participate-in-anti-terrorist-drill.html|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20111127083338/http://www.dawn.com/2011/11/26/pak-china-participate-in-anti-terrorist-drill.html|archivedate=27 November 2011|accessdate=11 March 2012|newspaper=Dawn|date=26 November 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|author=Kamran Yousaf|title=Joint military exercise: Pakistan, China begin war games near Jhelum|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/292020/joint-military-exercise-pakistan-china-begin-war-games-near-jhelum/|accessdate=11 March 2012|newspaper=Tribune|date=15 November 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; [[Philosophical]] basis for the [[Conscription|military draft]] is introduced by the [[Constitution of Pakistan|Constitution]] in times of emergency, but it has never been imposed.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.unhcr.org/refworld/country,,CSCOAL,,PAK,,486cb123c,0.html|title=Child Soldiers Global Report 2008 â€“ Pakistan|publisher=[[UNHCR]]|date=20 May 2008|accessdate=9 October 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; Since 1947, Pakistan has been involved in [[Indo-Pakistani wars and conflicts|four]] [[Conventional warfare|conventional wars]], the [[Indo-Pakistani war of 1947|first war]] occurred in [[Jammu and Kashmir|Kashmir]] with Pakistan gaining control of [[Western Kashmir]], ([[Azad Kashmir]] and [[Gilgitâ€“Baltistan]]), and India capturing [[Eastern Kashmir]] ([[Jammu and Kashmir]]). Territorial problems eventually led to another [[Indo-Pakistani war of 1965|conventional war]] in 1965; over the issue of [[East Bengali refugees|Bengali refugees]] that led to [[Indo-Pakistani war of 1971|another war]] in 1971 which resulted in Pakistan's [[Instrument of Surrender (1971)|unconditional surrender]] of [[East Pakistan]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=War History|url=http://www.pakistanarmy.gov.pk/AWPReview/TextContent.aspx?pId=47&amp;rnd=443|work=Pakistan Army|accessdate=24 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; Tensions in [[Kargil district|Kargil]] brought the two countries at the [[Indo-Pakistani War of 1999|brink of war]].&lt;ref name=&quot;kargil&quot; /&gt; Since 1947, the unresolved [[Durand Line|territorial problems]] with [[Afghanistan]] saw [[Afghanistanâ€“Pakistan skirmishes|border skirmishes]] which was kept mostly at the [[Afghanistan Pakistan border|mountainous border]]. In 1961, the military and [[Pakistani intelligence community|intelligence community]] repelled the [[Military history of Pakistan#Pakistan-Afghanistan border clash of 1961|Afghan incursion]] in the [[Bajaur Agency]] near the [[Durand Line]] border.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |title=Daoud as Prime Minister, 1953â€“63|url=http://lcweb2.loc.gov/cgi-bin/query/r?frd/cstdy:@field(DOCID+af0025)|year=1997|accessdate=6 November 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book|author=Ian Talbot|title=The Armed Forces of Pakistan|year=1999|publisher=Macmillan publishers|isbn=0-312-21606-8|page=99}}&lt;/ref&gt; Rising tensions with neighboring [[Soviet Union|USSR]] in [[Soviet war in Afghanistan|their involvement]] in [[Afghanistan]], Pakistani [[Pakistani intelligence community|intelligence community]], mostly the [[Inter-Services Intelligence|ISI]], [[Operation Cyclone|systematically coordinated]] the [[United States involvement in regime change|U.S. resources]] to the [[Afghan mujahideen]] and [[Afghan Arabs|foreign fighters]] against the [[Union of Soviet Socialist Republics (USSR)|Soviet Union]]'s presence in the region. Military reports indicated that the [[Pakistan Air Force|PAF]] was in engagement with the [[Soviet Air Forces|Soviet Air Force]], supported by the [[Afghan Air Force]] during the course of the [[Russian war in afghanistan|conflict]];&lt;ref name=&quot;PAF-History&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=HISTORY OF PAF|url=http://www.paf.gov.pk/history.html|publisher=Pakistan Air Force|accessdate=20 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; one of which belonged to [[Alexander Rutskoy]].&lt;ref name=&quot;PAF-History&quot; /&gt;

[[File:Pakistan Navy Ships2.jpeg|thumb|left| Pakistani Navy sailors in the [[Arabian Sea]].]]
Apart from its own conflicts, Pakistan has been an active [[United Nations peacekeeping missions involving Pakistan|participant in United Nations peacekeeping missions]]. It played a major role in rescuing trapped American soldiers from [[Mogadishu]], Somalia, in 1993 in [[Operation Gothic Serpent]].&lt;ref name=&quot;israel&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.defence.pk/pakistan-army/|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130822072041/http://www.defence.pk/pakistan-army/|archivedate=22 August 2013|title=Pakistan Army|publisher=Pakistan Defense|accessdate=11 March 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=UN Peace Keeping Missions|url=http://www.pakistanarmy.gov.pk/AWPReview/TextContent.aspx?pId=408&amp;rnd=497|publisher=Pakistan Army|accessdate=29 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; According to [[United Nations|UN]] reports, the Pakistani military are the largest troop contributors to UN [[UN peacekeeping missions involving Pakistan|peacekeeping missions]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=Monthly Summary of Contributors to UN Peacekeeping Operations|url=http://www.un.org/en/peacekeeping/contributors/2012/March12_1.pdf|publisher=United Nations|year=2012|page=2|accessdate=24 April 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pakistan sent UN Peacekeeping forces to the former Yugoslavia during the Yugoslav wars. During the war, Pakistan supported Bosnia while providing technical and military support. Approximately 90,000 Pakistani people went to Bosnia during the Yugoslav wars, accounting for 20% of the volunteer military force. The [[Inter-Services Intelligence]] (ISI) allegedly ran an active [[military intelligence]] program during the [[Bosnian War]] which started in 1992 lasting until 1995. Allegedly executed and supervised by [[Lieutenant-General|General]] [[Javed Nasir]], the program distributed and coordinated the systematic supply of arms to various groups of [[Bosnian mujahideen]] during the war.{{citation needed|date=September 2013}} The ISI Bosnian contingent was organized with [[Saudi foreign assistance|financial assistance provided by Saudi Arabia]], according to the British historian [[Mark Curtis (British author)|Mark Curtis]].&lt;ref name=&quot;Profile&quot;&gt;{{cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=KOMewMUw024C&amp;pg=PT109&amp;dq=isi+bosnia&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=SfObUafgA-qSiQKRp4D4Cg&amp;ved=0CDAQuwUwAA|title=Secret Affairs Britain's Collusion with Radical Islam.|last=Curtis|first=Mark|publisher=Profile|isbn=1847653014|edition=New updated|location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt; Despite the [[United Nations|UN]] arms embargo in [[Bosnia]], Nasir later confessed that the ISI airlifted anti-tank weapons and missiles to Bosnian mujahideen which turned the tide in favor of Bosnian Muslims and forced the Serbs to lift the siege.&lt;ref name=&quot;Press Trust of India&quot;&gt;{{cite news|url=http://expressindia.indianexpress.com/news/fullstory.php?newsid=17985|title='Pak defied UN, supplied arms to Bosnia'|date=4 September 2011|newspaper=Press Trust of India|accessdate=21 May 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;ISI Directorship&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.isi.org.pk/g.javed.htm|title=Javed Nasir|publisher=ISI Directorship|accessdate=21 May 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pakistan has [[Pakistan Armed Forces deployments|deployed its military]] in some [[Arab world|Arab countries]], providing defence, training, and playing advisory roles.&lt;ref name=&quot;Cordesman: Pakistani Toops at Tabuk&quot;&gt;{{cite book|author=Anthony H. Cordesman|title=Western Strategic Interests in Saudi Arabia|date=December 1986|publisher=Croom Helm|isbn=978-0-7099-4823-0|url=https://books.google.com/?id=vJQ9AAAAIAAJ&amp;printsec=frontcover#v=snippet&amp;q=Pakistani%20troops%20and%20advisors&amp;f=false|accessdate=22 April 2012|pages=139â€“140}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Chengappa: Military adviser&quot;&gt;{{cite book|url=https://books.google.com/?id=iDoMlBd4dYsC&amp;pg=PR2&amp;lpg=PR2&amp;dq=Pakistan,+Islamisation,+Army+and+Foreign+Policy#v=onepage&amp;q=advisers&amp;f=false|title=Pakistan Islamisation|date=30 November 2005|publisher=APH Publishing Corporation|isbn=978-81-7648-548-7|author=Bidanda M. Chengappa|accessdate=22 April 2012|page=42}}&lt;/ref&gt; The [[Pakistan Air Force|PAF]] and [[Pakistan Navy|Navy]]'s [[fighter pilot]]s have voluntarily served in [[Middle East|Arab nations]]' militaries against [[Israel]] in [[Six-Day War|the Six-Day War]] (1967) and in the [[Yom Kippur War]] (1973). Pakistan's [[fighter pilot]]s shot down ten Israeli planes in the Six-Day War.&lt;ref name=&quot;israel&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Pakistan Armed Forces|url=http://www.scramble.nl/pk.htm|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20011217224910/http://www.scramble.nl/pk.htm|archivedate=17 December 2001|publisher=Scramble Magazine|accessdate=24 July 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; In the 1973 war one of the PAF pilots, Flt. Lt. [[Sattar Alvi]] flying a MiG-21 shot down an Israeli Air Force Mirage and was honoured by the Syrian government.&lt;ref name=&quot;Chengappa2004&quot;&gt;{{cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=iDoMlBd4dYsC&amp;pg=PA42|title=Pakistan: Islamisation Army And Foreign Policy|date=1 January 2004|publisher=APH Publishing|isbn=978-81-7648-548-7|pages=42â€“|author=Bidanda M. Chengappa|accessdate=22 February 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Dunstan2003&quot;&gt;{{cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=1BYk_sXT6tsC&amp;pg=PA39|title=The Yom Kippur War 1973 (2): The Sinai|date=20 April 2003|publisher=Osprey Publishing|isbn=978-1-84176-221-0|pages=39â€“|author=Simon Dunstan|accessdate=22 February 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Kumaraswamy2013&quot;&gt;{{cite book|author=P.R. Kumaraswamy|title=Revisiting the Yom Kippur War|publisher=Routledge|isbn=978-1-136-32895-4|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=g1TkFQgzp5cC&amp;pg=PT75|accessdate=22 February 2013|date=11 January 2013|pages=75â€“}}&lt;/ref&gt; Requested by the [[Government of Saudi Arabia|Saudi monarchy]] in 1979, the [[Special Service Group|special forces]] units, operatives, and commandos were rushed to assist [[Saudi forces]] in [[Mecca]] to [[Grand Mosque Seizure|lead the operation]] of the [[Masjid al-Haram|Grand Mosque]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book|author=Irfan Husain|title=Fatal Faultlines : Pakistan, Islam and the West|year=2012|publisher=Arc Manor Publishers|location=Rockville, Maryland|isbn=978-1-60450-478-1|page=129|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=tNwzeQAHVJwC|accessdate=17 April 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; In 1991 Pakistan got involved with the [[Gulf War]] and sent 5,000 troops as part of a US-led coalition, specifically for the defence of [[Saudi Arabia]].&lt;ref name=&quot;gulf_war&quot;&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?f=/c/a/2002/09/24/MN168392.DTL&amp;ao=all|work=San Francisco Chronicle|date=24 September 2002|title=The 1991 Gulf war|accessdate=16 March 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Since 2004, the military has been engaged in a [[war in North-West Pakistan]], mainly against the homegrown [[Tehrik-i-Taliban Pakistan|Taliban factions]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/south_asia/3645114.stm|title=Pakistan's undeclared war|publisher=BBC|author=Zaffar Abbas|accessdate=19 October 2008|date=10 September 2004}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2006/01/24/AR2006012401528.html|title=The War in Pakistan|work=Washington Post|date=25 January 2006|accessdate=19 October 2008}}&lt;/ref&gt; Major operations undertaken by the Army include [[Operation Black Thunderstorm]] and [[Operation Rah-e-Nijat]].&lt;ref name=&quot;ashfaq&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.dawn.com/wps/wcm/connect/dawn-content-library/dawn/news/pakistan/04-jets-bomb-taliban-hideouts-swaziristan-qs-07|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20090620145347/http://www.dawn.com/wps/wcm/connect/dawn-content-library/dawn/news/pakistan/04-jets-bomb-taliban-hideouts-swaziristan-qs-07|archivedate=20 June 2009|title=Troops make gains in Swat and South Waziristan|date=21 June 2009|work=[[Dawn (newspaper)|Dawn]]|accessdate=29 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=26 killed as troops hit Taliban hideouts in Dir|url=http://www.dailytimes.com.pk/default.asp?page=2009\04\28\story_28-4-2009_pg1_3|accessdate=29 December 2011|newspaper=Daily Times|date=28 April 2009|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20090502160940/http://www.dailytimes.com.pk:80/default.asp?page=2009%5C04%5C28%5Cstory_28-4-2009_pg1_3|archivedate=2 May 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Kashmir conflict===
{{main article|Kashmir conflict}}
The [[Kashmir region|Kashmir]]â€“ the most northwesterly region of [[South Asia]]â€“ is a primary [[Kashmir problem|territorial dispute]] that hindered the [[India Pakistan relations|relations]] between [[India]] and Pakistan. [[India and Pakistan|Two nations]] have fought at least [[India Pakistan Wars|three large-scale]] [[Conventional warfare|conventional wars]] in successive years of [[Indo-Pakistani War of 1947|1947]], [[Indo-Pakistani War of 1965|1965]], and [[Indo-Pakistani War of 1971|1971]]. The [[Indo-Pakistani War of 1971|conflict]] in 1971 witnessed Pakistan's unconditional [[Instrument of Surrender (1971)|surrender]] and a [[Simla Agreement|treaty]] that subsequently led to the [[Independence of Bangladesh|independence]] of [[Bangladesh]].&lt;ref name=&quot;Lancer Publishers, 1996&quot;&gt;{{cite book|last1=Raza|first1=Maroof|title=Wars and no peace over Kashmir|date=1996|publisher=Lancer Publishers, 1996|location=New Delhi|isbn=1897829167|page=170|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=WyMwkTA9TyoC&amp;pg=PA58&amp;lpg=PA58&amp;dq=pakistan+lost+half+country&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=28rW9rM5w8&amp;sig=rfhD2NbOaasazGdRPY1YDrMWnfM&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=zAr9VJzjK831yAS0vYGwDA&amp;ved=0CEYQ6AEwCA#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=true|accessdate=9 March 2015|format=googlebooks|chapter=Â§Implications of 1971 war and India's nuclear explosion|quote={{small|&quot;In December 1971, Pakistan lost half its country, and with over ~90,000 troops of its military becoming [[Prisoner of War|POWs]], all its earlier myth could not survive this no longer...&quot;}}}}&lt;/ref&gt; Other serious military engagements and skirmishes included the armed contacts in [[Siachen conflict|Siachen Glacier]] (1984) and [[Kargil War|Kargil]] (1999).&lt;ref name=&quot;kashmir1&quot; /&gt; Approximately 45.1% of the [[Kashmir region]] is [[Indian controlled Kashmir|controlled]] by [[India]] while claiming the entire state of [[Kashmir and Jammu (princely state)|Jammu and Kashmir]], including most of [[Jammu]], the [[Kashmir Valley]], [[Ladakh]], and the [[Siachen Glacier|Siachen]].&lt;ref name=&quot;kashmir1&quot; /&gt; The claim is contested by Pakistan, which approximately [[Pakistani Controlled Kashmir|controls]] the 38.2% of the [[Kashmir region]], known as the [[Azad Kashmir]] and [[Gilgitâ€“Baltistan]].&lt;ref name=&quot;kashmir1&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book|author=Sean Anderson|title=Historical dictionary of terrorism|year=2009|publisher=Scarecrow Press|isbn=978-0-8108-4101-7|pages=347â€“348}}&lt;/ref&gt;
[[File:Shangrila Resorts.jpg|thumb|230px|left|Shangrila Resort, [[Skardu]], Gilgit-Baltistan]]
India claims the [[Kashmir]] on the basis of the [[Instrument of Accession (Jammu and Kashmir)|Instrument of Accession]]â€” a legal agreement with Kashmir's leaders executed by [[Ruler of Kashmir|''Maharaja'']] [[Maharaja Hari Singh|Hari Singh]] who agreed to accede the area to India.&lt;ref name=&quot;Commons&quot;&gt;{{cite web|author=Paul Bowers|title=Kashmir (House of Commons Research Paper 04/28)|date=30 March 2004|url=http://www.parliament.uk/documents/commons/lib/research/rp2004/rp04-028.pdf|page=46|publisher=House of Commons Library|accessdate=18 April 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pakistan claims [[Kashmir]] on the basis of a Muslim majority and of geography, the same principles that were applied for the creation of the two independent states.&lt;ref name=&quot;Amita Shastri South Asia&quot;&gt;{{cite book|author=Amita Shastri|title=The Post-Colonial States of South Asia: Democracy, Development and Identity|year=2001|publisher=Palgrave Macmillan|isbn=978-0-312-23852-0|page=289|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=du7xvBFpbg4C&amp;pg=PA289&amp;dq=Pakistan+claims+Kashmir+on+the+basis+of+a+Muslim+majority+and+geography#v=onepage&amp;q=Pakistan%20claims%20Kashmir%20on%20the%20basis%20of%20a%20Muslim%20majority%20and%20geography&amp;f=false|accessdate=15 March 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Joseph Regional Geography&quot;&gt;{{cite book|author=Joseph J. Hobbs|title=World Regional Geography|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=yAgGHnENHjoC&amp;printsec=frontcover&amp;dq=World+Regional+Geography#v=snippet&amp;q=Kashmir's&amp;f=false|accessdate=15 March 2012|year=2008|publisher=Brooks Cole|isbn=978-0-495-38950-7|page=314}}&lt;/ref&gt;  India referred the dispute to the United Nations on 1 January 1948.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|author=Auckland|title=A brief history of the Kashmir conflict|url=http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/1399992/A-brief-history-of-the-Kashmir-conflict.html|work=The Daily Telegraph|accessdate=23 January 2012|date=24 September 2001|location=London}}&lt;/ref&gt; A [[United Nations Security Council Resolution 38|resolution]] passed in 1948, the [[United Nations|UN]]'s [[Un security council|General Assembly]] asked Pakistan to remove most of its troops as a [[Plebiscite in Kashmir|''plebiscite'']] would then be held. However, Pakistan failed to vacate the region and a [[ceasefire]] was reached in 1949 with the [[Line of Control]] (LoC) was established, dividing Kashmir between the [[India and Pakistan|two nations]].&lt;ref name=&quot;kash&quot;&gt;{{cite web|author=International Court of Justice|title=Advisory Opinion on the Legal Status of Kashmir|url=http://imuna.org/nhsmun/committee/international-court-justice-2012|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20111011211119/http://imuna.org/nhsmun/committee/international-court-justice-2012|archivedate=11 October 2011|year=2012|publisher=[[IMUNA]]|accessdate=23 January 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; India, fearful that the Muslim majority populace of Kashmir would secede from India, did not allow a plebiscite to take place in the region. This was confirmed in a statement by India's Defense Minister, Kirshnan Menon, who said: &quot;Kashmir would vote to join Pakistan and no Indian Government responsible for agreeing to plebiscite would survive.&lt;nowiki&gt;''&lt;/nowiki&gt;&lt;ref&gt;Endrst, Jeff (September 8, 1965). &quot;Kashmir Old Headache For U.N&quot;. ''The Pittsburgh Press''. Retrieved 8/02/2016.&lt;/ref&gt;

Pakistan claims that its position is for the right of the [[Kashmiri people|people]] of [[Jammu and Kashmir]] to determine their future through impartial elections as mandated by the [[United Nations]],&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|author=Talat Masood|title=Pakistan's Kashmir Policy|url=http://www.silkroadstudies.org/new/docs/CEF/Quarterly/November_2006/Masood.pdf|format=PDF|year=2006|publisher=Central Asia-Caucasus Institute &amp; Silk Road Studies Program|page=1|accessdate=19 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; while India has stated that [[Kashmir]] is an [[Akhand Bharat|integral part]] of India, referring to the [[Simla Agreement]](1972) and to the fact that [[Elections in India|elections]] take place regularly.&lt;ref name=&quot;unhcr2009in&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.unhcr.org/refworld/country,,,ANNUALREPORT,IND,,4a6452aa2d,0.html|title=Freedom in the World 2009&amp;nbsp;â€“ Kashmir (India)|date=16 July 2009|publisher=[[UNHCR]]|accessdate=1 May 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; In recent developments, certain Kashmiri [[Kashmir independence movement|independence groups]] believe that Kashmir should be independent of both [[India and Pakistan]].&lt;ref name=&quot;kashmir1&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/312908/Kashmir/214223/The-Kashmir-problem#ref673547|title=Kashmir|publisher=EncyclopÃ¦dia Britannica|accessdate=19 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===Law enforcement===
{{main article|Law enforcement in Pakistan|Pakistan Intelligence Community|National Intelligence Directorate}}

The [[Law enforcement in Pakistan|law enforcement]] in Pakistan is carried out by joint network of several federal and provincial police agencies. The [[Administrative units of Pakistan|four provinces]] and the [[Islamabad Capital Territory]] each have a civilian police force with jurisdiction extending only to the relevant province or territory.&lt;ref name=&quot;ciafactbook&quot; /&gt; At the federal level, there are a number of civilian [[Pakistan Intelligence Community|intelligence agencies]] with nationwide jurisdictions including the [[Federal Investigation Agency]] (FIA), [[Intelligence Bureau (Pakistan)|Intelligence Bureau]] (IB), and the [[National Highways and Motorway Police|Motoway Patrol]], as well as several [[Paramilitary forces of Pakistan|paramilitary forces]] such as the [[National Guard of Pakistan|National Guards]] ([[Northern Areas of Pakistan|Northern Areas]]), the [[pakistan Rangers|Rangers]] ([[Punjab, Pakistan|Punjab]] and [[Sindh]]), and the [[Frontier Corps]] ([[Khyber Pakhtunkhwa|Khyber-Pakhtunkhwa]] and [[Balochistan, Pakistan|Balochistan]]).

The most senior officers of all the civilian police forces also form part of the [[Police Service of Pakistan|Police Service]], which is a component of the [[Central Superior Services of Pakistan|civil service]] of Pakistan. Namely, there are [[Administrative units of Pakistan|four provincial]] [[Police Service of Pakistan|police service]] including the [[Punjab Police (Pakistan)|Punjab Police]], [[Sindh Police]], [[Khyber Pakhtunkhwa Police|Khyber-Pakhtunkhwa Police]], and the [[Balochistan Police]]; all headed by the appointed senior [[Inspector general|Inspector-Generals]]. The [[Islamabad Capital Territory|Islamabad]] has its own police component, the [[Capital Territory Police|Capital Police]], to maintain [[Law and order (politics)|law and order]] in the capital. The [[Crime Investigation Department (Pakistan)|CID]] bureaus are the [[crime investigation]] unit and forms a vital part in each provincial [[Police Service of Pakistan|police service]].

The [[Law enforcement in Pakistan|law enforcement]] in Pakistan also has a [[National Highways &amp; Motorway Police|Motorway Patrol]] which is responsible for enforcement of traffic and safety laws, security and recovery on Pakistan's inter-provincial [[Motorways of Pakistan|motorway network]]. In each of provincial [[Police Service of Pakistan|Police Service]], it also maintains a respective [[Elite Police]] units led by the [[National Counter Terrorism Authority|NACTA]]â€“ a counter-terrorism police unit as well as providing [[Very Important Person|VIP escorts]]. In [[Punjab, Pakistan|Punjab]] and [[Sindh]], the [[Pakistan Rangers]] are an internal security force with the prime objective to provide and maintain security in war zones and areas of conflict as well as maintaining law and order which includes providing assistance to the police.&lt;ref name=&quot;npb1&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.npb.gov.pk/partners/|title=Our Partners|publisher=National Police Bureau, Government of Pakistan|accessdate=1 July 2008|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20120118155449/http://www.npb.gov.pk/partners/|archivedate=18 January 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; The [[Frontier Corps]] serves the similar purpose in [[Khyber Pakhtunkhwa|Khyber-Pakhtunkhwa]], and the [[Balochistan, Pakistan|Balochistan]].&lt;ref name=&quot;npb1&quot; /&gt;

==Geography, environment and climate==
{{Main article|List of extreme weather records in Pakistan|l1=Extreme weather records in Pakistan|Geography of Pakistan|Environment of Pakistan|Climate of Pakistan|Tropical cyclones and tornadoes in Pakistan|List of beaches in Pakistan}}
[[File:Pakistan map of KÃ¶ppen climate classification.svg|thumb|300px|Pakistan map of KÃ¶ppen climate classification.]]
The [[Geography of Pakistan|geography]] and [[Climate of Pakistan|climate]] of Pakistan are extremely diverse, and the country is home to a wide variety of [[wildlife]].&lt;ref name=&quot;Ministry of Information, Broadcasting, and National Heritage&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Land and People|url=http://infopak.gov.pk/LandAndPeople.aspx|website=http://infopak.gov.pk/|publisher=Ministry of Information, Broadcasting, and National Heritage|accessdate=18 February 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pakistan covers an area of {{convert|796095|km2|abbr=on}}, approximately equal to the combined land areas of France and the United Kingdom. It is the [[List of countries by area|36th largest nation by total area]], although this ranking varies depending on how the disputed territory of Kashmir is counted. Pakistan has a {{convert|1046|km|abbr=on}} coastline along the Arabian Sea and the Gulf of Oman in the south&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=PNS Gwadar|url=http://www.globalsecurity.org/military/world/pakistan/pns-gwadar.htm|publisher=Global Security|date=21 November 2011|accessdate=4 January 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; and land borders of {{convert|6774|km|abbr=on}} in total: {{convert|2430|km|abbr=on}} with Afghanistan, {{convert|523|km|abbr=on}} with China, {{convert|2912|km|abbr=on}} with India and {{convert|909|km|abbr=on}} with Iran.&lt;ref name=&quot;ciafactbook&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/geos/pk.html|title=Pakistan|publisher=[[Central Intelligence Agency|CIA]]|work=[[World Factbook]]|accessdate=13 February 2008}}&lt;/ref&gt; It shares a marine border with Oman,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.un.org/Depts/los/LEGISLATIONANDTREATIES/PDFFILES/TREATIES/OMN-PAK2000MB.PDF|title=Muscat Agreement on the Delimitation of the Maritime Boundary between the Sultanate of Oman and the Islamic Republic of Pakistan, 12 June 2000(1)|page=1|accessdate=18 August 2011|work=United Nations}}&lt;/ref&gt; and is separated from Tajikistan by the cold, narrow [[Wakhan Corridor]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|author=Edward Wong|title=In Icy Tip of Afghanistan, War Seems Remote|url=http://www.nytimes.com/2010/10/28/world/asia/28wakhan.html|accessdate=4 January 2012|newspaper=New York Times|date=27 October 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pakistan occupies a geopolitically important location at the crossroads of South Asia, the Middle East and Central Asia.&lt;ref name=&quot;yasmeen&quot; /&gt;

Geologically, Pakistan is located in the Indus-Tsangpo Suture Zone and overlaps the [[Indian plate|Indian tectonic plate]] in its Sindh and Punjab provinces; Balochistan and most of Khyber Pakhtunkhwa are within the [[Eurasian plate]], mainly on the [[Iranian plateau]]. Gilgitâ€“Baltistan and Azad Kashmir lie along the edge of the Indian plate and hence are [[List of earthquakes in Pakistan|prone to violent earthquakes]]. This region has the highest rates of seismicity and largest earthquakes in the Himalaya region.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Pakistan in the most active quake zone, says US Geological Survey|url=http://www.dawn.com/news/1215636/pakistan-in-the-most-active-quake-zone-says-us-geological-survey|work=[[Dawn]]|accessdate=5 November 2015|date=27 October 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Ranging from the coastal areas of the south to the glaciated mountains of the north, Pakistan's landscapes vary from plains to deserts, forests, hills and plateaus .&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|year=2010|title=Pakistan|url=http://www.fao.org/nr/water/aquastat/countries_regions/pakistan/index.stm|publisher=Food and Agriculture Organisation of the United Nations|accessdate=29 December 2011|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20111222051452/http://www.fao.org/nr/water/aquastat/countries_regions/pakistan/index.stm|archivedate=22 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pakistan is divided into three major geographic areas: the northern highlands, the [[Indus River]] plain and the Balochistan Plateau.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=About Pakistan: Geography|url=http://www.pakistanstudies-aips.org/pakistan/geography/index.html|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110721035911/http://www.pakistanstudies-aips.org/pakistan/geography/index.html|archivedate=21 July 2011|publisher=American Institute For Pakistan Studies|accessdate=24 July 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; The northern highlands contain the [[Karakoram]], [[Hindu Kush]] and [[Pamir Mountains|Pamir]] mountain ranges (see [[mountains of Pakistan]]), which contain some of the world's highest peaks, including five of the fourteen [[eight-thousanders]] (mountain peaks over {{convert|8000|m|ft|-1||disp=or}}), which attract adventurers and mountaineers from all over the world, notably [[K2]] ({{convert|8611|m|abbr=on|disp=or}}) and [[Nanga Parbat]] ({{convert|8126|m|abbr=on|disp=or}}).&lt;ref name=&quot;mountains&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.tourism.gov.pk/mountain.html|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20061110014044/http://www.tourism.gov.pk/mountain.html|archivedate=10 November 2006|title=PTDC page on mountaineering|publisher=Pakistan Tourism Development Corporation|accessdate=10 November 2006}}{{dead link|date=October 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; The Balochistan Plateau lies in the west and the [[Thar Desert]] in the east. The {{convert|1609|km|abbr=on}} Indus River and its tributaries flow through the country from the Kashmir region to the Arabian Sea. There is an expanse of alluvial plains along it in Punjab and Sindh.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.infoplease.com/ipa/A0107861.html|title=Pakistan|work=InfoPlease|publisher=Pearson Education|accessdate=16 March 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The climate varies from tropical to temperate, with arid conditions in the coastal south. There is a [[monsoon]] season with frequent flooding due to heavy rainfall, and a dry season with significantly less rainfall or none at all. There are four distinct seasons: a cool, dry winter from December through February; a hot, dry spring from March through May; the summer rainy season, or southwest monsoon period, from June through September; and the retreating monsoon period of October and November.&lt;ref name=&quot;congress&quot; /&gt; Rainfall varies greatly from year to year, and patterns of alternate flooding and drought are common.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.nationsencyclopedia.com/Asia-and-Oceania/Pakistan-CLIMATE.html|title=Pakistan Climate|publisher=Encyclopedia of the Nations|date=28 March 2008|accessdate=16 March 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;
&lt;gallery mode=&quot;packed&quot; heights=&quot;120px&quot; widths=&quot;px&quot;&gt;

===Flora and fauna===
{{Main article|Flora of Pakistan|Fauna of Pakistan}}
[[File:Pedrengo cedro nel parco Frizzoni.jpg|thumb|[[Cedrus deodara|Deodar]],{{efn|{{lang-ur|{{nq|Ø¯ÛŒÙˆØ¯Ø§Ø±}}|link=no}} [[ALA-LC]]: {{transl|Urdu|ALA-LC|''DiyodÄ?r''}}}} Pakistan's national tree.]]
The diversity of landscapes and climates in Pakistan allows a wide variety of trees and plants to flourish. The forests range from coniferous [[alpine plant|alpine]] and [[subalpine]] trees such as [[spruce]], [[pine]] and [[deodar cedar]] in the extreme northern mountains, through [[deciduous]] trees in most of the country (for example the mulberry-like [[Dalbergia sissoo|shisham]] found in the [[Sulaiman Mountains]]), to palms such as [[coconut]] and [[Phoenix dactylifera|date]] in southern Punjab, southern Balochistan and all of Sindh. The western hills are home to [[juniper]], [[tamarisk]], coarse grasses and scrub plants. [[Mangrove]] forests form much of the coastal wetlands along the coast in the south.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://wwfpak.org/forest_mangrove.php|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20041225000128/http://wwfpak.org/forest_mangrove.php|archivedate=25 December 2004|title=Conservation of Mangrove Forests in the Coastal Areas of Sindh and Balochistan|work=WWF Pakistan|accessdate=17 March 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Coniferous forests are found at altitudes ranging from 1,000 to 4,000 metres in most of the northern and northwestern highlands. In the [[xeric]] regions of Balochistan, date palm and ''[[Ephedra (genus)|Ephedra]]'' are common. In most of Punjab and Sindh, the Indus plains support tropical and subtropical dry and moist broadleaf forestry as well as tropical and xeric shrublands. These forests are mostly of [[mulberry]], [[acacia]], and [[eucalyptus]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=Introduction|url=http://www.rrcap.unep.org/lc/cd/html/countryrep/pakistan/introduction.html|work=AIT-UNEP RRC.AP|accessdate=27 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; About 2.2% or {{convert|1687000|ha|km2}} of Pakistan was forested in 2010.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|author=Rhett Butler|url=http://rainforests.mongabay.com/deforestation/2000/Pakistan.htm|title=Pakistan Deforestation Rates and Related Forestry Figures|work=Mongabay.com|accessdate=19 April 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The fauna of Pakistan reflects its varied climates too. Around 668 bird species are found there:&lt;ref name=&quot;wwf11&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;bio&quot; /&gt; [[crow]]s, [[sparrow]]s, [[Acridotheres|mynas]], [[hawk]]s, [[falcon]]s and [[eagle]]s commonly occur. [[Palas, Kohistan]], has a significant population of [[western tragopan]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite journal|author=[[Naeem Ashraf Raja]], P. Davidson|year=1999|title=The birds of Palas, North-West Frontier Province, Pakistan|url=http://www.orientalbirdclub.org/publications/forktail/15pdfs/Raja-Palas.pdf|journal=Forktail|volume=15|pages=77â€“85|publisher=Oriental Bird Club|accessdate=12 November 2011|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20110610214757/http://www.orientalbirdclub.org/publications/forktail/15pdfs/Raja-Palas.pdf|archivedate=10 June 2011|display-authors=etal}}&lt;/ref&gt; Many birds sighted in Pakistan are migratory, coming from Europe, Central Asia and India.&lt;ref name=&quot;GrimmettRoberts2009&quot;&gt;{{cite book|title=Birds of Pakistan|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=OoeL2O5Iq0YC|publisher=A&amp;C Black|accessdate=11 January 2012|author1=Richard Grimmett|author2=Tom J. Roberts|author3=Tim Inskipp|date=27 February 2009|isbn=978-0-7136-8800-9|pages=6,38â€“41,132â€“136}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The southern plains are home to [[mongoose]]s, [[civet]]s, hares, the [[Asiatic jackal]], the [[Indian pangolin]], the [[jungle cat]] and the [[desert cat]]. There are [[mugger crocodile]]s in the Indus, and [[wild boar]], deer, [[porcupine]]s and small rodents are common in the surrounding areas. The sandy scrublands of central Pakistan are home to Asiatic jackals, [[striped hyena]]s, wildcats and [[leopards]].&lt;ref name=&quot;sheet&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Sheet1|url=http://www.wwfpak.org/images/listmammalsofpakistan.xls|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20060915012052/http://www.wwfpak.org/images/listmammalsofpakistan.xls|archivedate=15 September 2006|format=XLS|publisher=WWF|accessdate=11 January 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;animal&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Pakistan plant and animal life|url=http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/438805/Pakistan/23683/Plant-and-animal-life|publisher=EncyclopÃ¦dia Britannica|accessdate=27 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; The lack of vegetative cover, the severe climate and the impact of grazing on the deserts have left wild animals in a precarious position. The [[chinkara]] is the only animal that can still be found in significant numbers in [[Cholistan]]. A small number of [[nilgai]] are found along the Pakistan-India border and in some parts of Cholistan.&lt;ref name=&quot;sheet&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;ShackletonGroup1997&quot;&gt;{{cite book|title=Wild sheep and goats and their relatives: status survey and conservation action plan for caprinae|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=hJBodAXB9eoC&amp;pg=PA243|accessdate=11 January 2012|author1=David M. Shackleton|author2=International Union for Conservation of Nature and Natural Resources. Species Survival Commission. Caprinae Specialist Group|date=January 1997|publisher=IUCN|isbn=978-2-8317-0353-4|pages=10â€“13, 352}}&lt;/ref&gt; A wide variety of animals live in the mountainous north, including the [[Marco Polo sheep]], the [[urial]] (a subspecies of wild sheep), [[markhor]] and [[ibex]] goats, the [[Asian black bear]] and the [[Himalayan brown bear]].&lt;ref name=&quot;sheet&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;wwf&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Species|url=http://wwfpak.org/species/index.php|work=WWF Pakistan|accessdate=27 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;wes&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Pakistan|url=http://www.wcs.org/where-we-work/asia/pakistan.aspx|work=Wildlife Conservation Society|accessdate=27 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; Among the rare animals found in the area are the [[snow leopard]],&lt;ref name=&quot;wwf&quot; /&gt; the [[Asiatic cheetah]]&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=Asiatic Cheetah|url=http://wwfpak.org/sc_asiaticcheetah.php|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20050421164349/http://wwfpak.org/sc_asiaticcheetah.php|archivedate=21 April 2005|work=WWF Pakistan|accessdate=27 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; and the blind [[Indus river dolphin]], of which there are believed to be about 1,100 remaining, protected at the Indus River Dolphin Reserve in Sindh.&lt;ref name=&quot;wwf&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Heiden&quot;&gt;{{cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=0RQwcO0wM6IC&amp;pg=PA33 |title=Pakistan |publisher=ABDO |accessdate=11 January 2012 |author=Pete Heiden|isbn=978-1-61787-631-8|pages=33â€“44|date=1 September 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; In total, 174 mammals, 177 reptiles, 22 amphibians, 198 freshwater fish species and 5,000 species of invertebrates (including insects) have been recorded in Pakistan.&lt;ref name=&quot;wwf11&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;bio&quot; /&gt;

The flora and fauna of Pakistan suffer from a number of problems. Pakistan has the second-highest rate of deforestation in the world. This, along with hunting and pollution, is causing adverse effects on the ecosystem. The government has established a large number of protected areas, wildlife sanctuaries, and game reserves to deal with these issues.&lt;ref name=&quot;wwf11&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Biodiversity|url=http://wwfpak.org/p_environment_biodiversity.php|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20050115084804/http://wwfpak.org/p_environment_biodiversity.php|archivedate=15 January 2005|publisher=WWF|accessdate=10 January 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;bio&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Biodiversity Sharing the Environment|url=http://www.environment.gov.pk/pub-pdf/StateER2005/Part3-Chp%205.pdf|publisher=Government of Pakistan|pages=1, 4â€“7|accessdate=10 January 2012|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20060827071639/http://www.environment.gov.pk:80/pub-pdf/StateER2005/Part3-Chp%205.pdf|archivedate=27 August 2006}}&lt;/ref&gt;

===National parks and wildlife sanctuaries===
{{Main article|Protected areas of Pakistan|National parks of Pakistan}}
[[File:Deosai Plateau 2.jpg|thumb|Plain of [[Deosai National Park]].]]
As of present, there are around 157 [[protected area]]s in Pakistan that are recognized by [[IUCN]]. According to the 'Modern Protected Areas' legislation, a national park is a protected area set aside by the [[Government of Pakistan|government]] for the protection and conservation of its outstanding scenery and wildlife in a natural state. The oldest national park is [[Lal Suhanra National Park|Lal Suhanra]] in [[Bahawalpur District]], established in 1972.&lt;ref name=&quot;cjpas_june_2010&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://cjpas.net/current_issue.pdf|title=Canadian Journal of Pure and Applied Sciences, an international journal: Current issue (Number: 4, Volume: 2, June 2010) Online ISSN 1920-3853|publisher=SENRA Academic Publishers, Burnaby, British Columbia|work=cjpas.net|year=2010|accessdate=September 8, 2010|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20110616210536/http://cjpas.net:80/current_issue.pdf|archivedate=16 June 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; It is also the only [[biosphere reserve]] of Pakistan. Lal Suhanra is the only national park established before the [[History of Pakistan#Independence of Pakistan|independence]] of the nation in August 1947. [[Central Karakoram National Park|Central Karakoram]] in [[Gilgit Baltistan]] is currently the largest national park in the country, spanning over a total approximate area of {{convert|1390100|ha|acre|1|sortable=on}}. The smallest national park is the [[Ayub National Park|Ayub]], covering a total approximate area of {{convert|931|ha|acre|1|sortable=on}}.

==Infrastructure==

===Economy===
{{Main article|Economy of Pakistan|Economic history of Pakistan}}

==== Overview ====
[[File:Karachi_sky_line.jpg|thumb|right|300px|[[Karachi]], the largest city of Pakistan.]]
[[File:Long Exposure of Blue Area Islamabad.JPG|thumb|right|300px|[[Islamabad]], the capital city of Pakistan.]]
Economists estimate that Pakistan has been part of the wealthiest [[Indian subcontinent|region]] of the world throughout the first millennium CE having the largest economy by GDP. This advantage was lost in the 18th century as other regions edged forward such as China and Western Europe.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite book|title=The World Economy. A Millennial Perspective (Vol. 1). Historical Statistics (Vol. 2)|last=Maddison|first=Angus|publisher=OECD|year=2006|isbn=92-64-02261-9|location=|pages=241,&amp;nbsp;261}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pakistan is considered as a [[developing country]]&lt;ref name=&quot;gulfmedia&quot;&gt;{{cite web|author=Faryal Leghari|url=http://www.grc.ae/?frm_module=contents&amp;frm_action=detail_book&amp;sec=Contents&amp;override=Articles%20%3E%20GCC%20Investments%20in%20Pakistan%20and%20Future%20Trends&amp;book_id=25458&amp;op_lang=en|title=GCC investments in Pakistan and future trends|publisher=Gulf Research Center|date=3 January 2007|accessdate=12 February 2008}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;mcb&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.mcb.com.pk/quick_links/pdf/Quid%20Pro%20Quo%2045%20Tales%20of%20Success.pdf|title=Quid Pro Quo 45&amp;nbsp;â€“ Tales of Success|publisher=Muslim Commercial Bank of Pakistan |accessdate=12 February 2008|format=PDF|year=2007|page=2|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20080216025016/http://www.mcb.com.pk/quick_links/pdf/Quid%20Pro%20Quo%2045%20Tales%20of%20Success.pdf|archivedate=16 February 2008}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;bbcbusiness&quot;&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/business/5007680.stm|title=Pakistan steels itself for sell-offs|publisher=BBC News|date=1 June 2006|accessdate=12 February 2008|author=Malcolm Borthwick}}&lt;/ref&gt; and is one of the [[Next Eleven]], the eleven countries that, along with the [[BRIC]]s, have a high potential to become the world's largest economies in the 21st century.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|author=Tavia Grant|title=On 10th birthday, BRICs poised for more growth|url=http://www.theglobeandmail.com/report-on-business/economy/economy-lab/daily-mix/on-10th-birthday-brics-poised-for-more-growth/article2264208/|accessdate=4 January 2012|newspaper=The Globe and Mail|date=8 December 2011|location=Toronto}}&lt;/ref&gt; However, after decades of social instability, {{As of|2013|lc=y}}, serious deficiencies in [[Macromanagement|macromangament]] and unbalanced [[macroeconomics]] in basic services such as [[Railways in Pakistan|train transportation]] and [[Electricity in Pakistan|electrical energy]] generation had developed.&lt;ref name=&quot;NYT51813&quot;&gt;{{cite news|title=Pakistan, Rusting in Its Tracks|url=http://www.nytimes.com/2013/05/19/world/asia/pakistans-railroads-sum-up-nations-woes.html|accessdate=19 May 2013|newspaper=The New York Times|date=18 May 2013|author=Declan Walsh|quote=natural disasters and entrenched insurgencies, abject poverty and feudal kleptocrats, and an economy near meltdown}}&lt;/ref&gt; The economy is considered to be semi-industrialized, with centres of growth along the [[Indus River]].&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite journal |last1=Henneberry|first1=S.|doi=10.1016/S0169-5150(99)00041-9|title=An analysis of industrialâ€“agricultural interactions: A case study in Pakistan|journal=Agricultural Economics|volume=22|pages=17â€“27|year=2000|pmid=|pmc=}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;siteresources.worldbank.org&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://siteresources.worldbank.org/PAKISTANEXTN/Resources/293051-1241610364594/6097548-1257441952102/balochistaneconomicreportvol2.pdf|title=World Bank Document|format=PDF|year=2008|page=14|accessdate=2 January 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;raid&quot; /&gt; The diversified economies of [[Economy of Karachi|Karachi]] and [[Economy of Punjab, Pakistan|Punjab's urban centres]] coexist with less developed areas in other parts of the country particularly in [[Balochistan, Pakistan|Balochistan]].&lt;ref name=&quot;siteresources.worldbank.org&quot; /&gt; Pakistan is the 70th largest export economy in the world and the 89th most complex economy according to the [[Economic complexity index]] (ECI). In 2013, Pakistan exported $28.2B and imported $44.8B, resulting in a negative trade balance of $16.6B.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://atlas.media.mit.edu/en/profile/country/pak/|title=OEC   â€“ Pakistan (PAK) Exports, Imports, and Trade Partners|website=atlas.media.mit.edu|access-date=2016-03-24}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pakistan's estimated [[nominal GDP]] {{As of|2016|lc=y}} is US$271 billion making it the 41st largest in the world and second largest in South Asia representing about 15.0% of [[South Asia|regional GDP]].&lt;ref name=&quot;raid&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;Recent developments&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Recent developments|url=http://web.worldbank.org/WBSITE/EXTERNAL/EXTDEC/EXTDECPROSPECTS/EXTGBLPROSPECTSAPRIL/0,,contentMDK:20394787~menuPK:659178~pagePK:2470434~piPK:4977459~theSitePK:659149,00.html|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120120030342/http://web.worldbank.org/WBSITE/EXTERNAL/EXTDEC/EXTDECPROSPECTS/EXTGBLPROSPECTSAPRIL/0,,contentMDK:20394787~menuPK:659178~pagePK:2470434~piPK:4977459~theSitePK:659149,00.html|archivedate=20 January 2012|publisher=The World Bank|date=June 2011|accessdate=30 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;bloomberg.com&quot;&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bloomberg.com/apps/news?pid=newsarchive&amp;sid=aJxFBbyVC_hs|title=Pakistan May Keep Key Rate Unchanged After Two Cuts This Year|publisher=Bloomberg|date=28 September 2009|accessdate=2 January 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; The [[GDP]] by [[Purchasing power parity|PPP]] is [[US dollar|US$]]838,164 million.&lt;ref&gt;[http://databank.worldbank.org/data/download/GDP_PPP.pdf GDP ranking, PPP based World Bank]&lt;/ref&gt; The estimated nominal [[per capita GDP]] is [[US dollar|US$]]1,197, [[GDP (PPP) per capita|GDP (PPP)/capita]] is [[US dollar|US$]]4,602 ([[international dollar]]s), and [[debt-to-GDP ratio]] is 55.5%.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|title=Report for Selected Countries and Subjects|url=http://www.imf.org/external/pubs/ft/weo/2011/01/weodata/weorept.aspx?sy=2008&amp;ey=2011&amp;scsm=1&amp;ssd=1&amp;sort=country&amp;ds=.&amp;br=1&amp;c=564&amp;s=NGDPD%2CNGDPDPC%2CPPPGDP%2CPPPPC%2CLP&amp;grp=0&amp;a=&amp;pr.x=52&amp;pr.y=8|publisher=International Monetary Fund|date=April 2011|accessdate=30 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|title=Economic Survey 2010â€“11: Country sinks deeper into debt|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/181368/economic-survey-2010-11-country-sinks-deeper-into-debt/|accessdate=30 December 2011|newspaper=Express Tribune|date=3 June 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; According to the [[World Bank]], Pakistan has important strategic endowments and development potential. The increasing proportion of Pakistan's youth provides the country with a potential demographic dividend and a challenge to provide adequate services and employment.&lt;ref name=&quot;auto&quot; /&gt; 21.04% of the population live below the international poverty line of US$1.25 a day. Unemployment rate among aged 15 and over population is 5.5%.&lt;ref name=&quot;poor&quot;&gt;{{cite web|title=Human Development Indices|url=http://hdr.undp.org/en/media/HDI_2008_EN_Tables.pdf|publisher=United Nations Development Programme, Human Development Reports|format=PDF|page=15|accessdate=6 October 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pakistan has an estimated of 40 million [[middle class]] citizens which are projected to increase to 100 million people by 2050.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://www.forbes.com/sites/danielrunde/2016/02/29/us-higher-education-partnership-development-pakistan/#11d078c1d7dd|title=How U.S. Higher Education Partnerships Can Promote Development In Pakistan|website=Forbes|access-date=2016-03-04}}&lt;/ref&gt; A 2013 report published by the [[World Bank]] positioned Pakistan's economy at 24th largest in the world by purchasing power and 45th largest in absolute dollars.&lt;ref name=&quot;raid&quot; /&gt; It is South Asia's second largest economy, representing about 15.0% of [[South Asia|regional GDP]].&lt;ref name=&quot;Recent developments&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;bloomberg.com&quot; /&gt; 
{| class=&quot;wikitable sortable infobox&quot;

Pakistan's economic growth since its inception has been varied. It has been slow during periods of [[Democracy in Pakistan|democratic transition]], but excellent during the three periods of [[Martial law in Pakistan|martial law]], although the foundation for sustainable and equitable growth was not formed.&lt;ref name=&quot;ChowdhuryMahmud2008&quot; /&gt; The early to middle 2000s was a period of [[Economic liberalisation in Pakistan|rapid economic reforms]]; the government raised development spending, which reduced poverty levels by 10% and increased GDP by 3%.&lt;ref name=&quot;ciafactbook&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;JohnWall2006&quot;&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.worldbank.org.pk/WBSITE/EXTERNAL/COUNTRIES/SOUTHASIAEXT/PAKISTANEXTN/0,,contentMDK:20918063~menuPK:293074~pagePK:2865066~piPK:2865079~theSitePK:293052,00.html|title=Concluding Remarks at the Pakistan Development Forum 2006|author=John Wall|publisher=World Bank|accessdate=30 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; The economy cooled again from 2007.&lt;ref name=&quot;ciafactbook&quot; /&gt; Inflation reached 25.0% in 2008&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|author=Sajid Chaudhry|title=Inflation Outlook 2008â€“09:|url=http://www.dailytimes.com.pk/default.asp?page=2009\01\17\story_17-1-2009_pg5_2|accessdate=30 December 2011|newspaper=Daily Times|date=17 January 2009|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20120111205343/http://www.dailytimes.com.pk/default.asp?page=2009%5C01%5C17%5Cstory_17-1-2009_pg5_2|archivedate=11 January 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; and Pakistan had to depend on a fiscal policy backed by the [[International Monetary Fund]] to avoid possible bankruptcy.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.telegraph.co.uk/finance/financetopics/financialcrisis/3147266/Pakistan-facing-bankruptcy.html|title=Pakistan facing bankruptcyâ€”Telegraph|accessdate=6 October 2008|author=Isambard Wilkinson|work=The Daily Telegraph|location=London|date=6 October 2008}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite news|url=http://www.telegraph.co.uk/comment/columnists/concoughlin/3562715/If-Pakistan-goes-bust-the-Taliban-will-rule-the-roost-there-as-well.html|title=If Pakistan goes bust, the Taliban will rule the roost there as wellâ€”Telegraph|accessdate=10 October 2008|author=Con Coughlin|work=The Daily Telegraph|location=London|date=10 October 2008}}&lt;/ref&gt; A year later, the [[Asian Development Bank]] reported that Pakistan's economic crisis was easing.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.dawn.com.pk/wps/wcm/connect/dawn-content-library/dawn/news/business/09-pakistans-economic-crisis-eases-in-2009-adb--szh-06|title=Business &amp;#124; Pakistan's economic crisis eases in 2009: ADB|work=Dawn|location=Pakistan|date=23 September 2009|accessdate=2 January 2010}}{{dead link|date=May 2016|bot=medic}}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}&lt;/ref&gt; The inflation rate for the fiscal year {{nowrap|2010â€“11}} was 14.1%.&lt;ref name=&quot;edu&quot; /&gt; Since 2013, as part of an [[International Monetary Fund]] program Pakistan's economic growth has picked up. [[Goldman Sachs]] predicted, in 2014, that Pakistan's economy would grow 15 times in the next 35 years to become 18th largest economy in the world by 2050.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/660936/global-ranking-pakistan-billed-to-become-18th-largest-economy-by-2050/|title=Global ranking: Pakistan billed to become 18th largest economy by 2050 â€“ The Express Tribune|website=The Express Tribune|language=en-US|access-date=2016-03-04}}&lt;/ref&gt; On January 2014, a survey conducted by the ''[[Japan External Trade Organization]]'' placed Pakistan just behind [[Taiwan]] in terms of business generated by Japanese companies. Pakistan's data was generated from 27 Japanese firms doing business here. The results found that 74.1% of the Japanese companies estimated operating profit in 2013.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/666147/business-growth-jetro-survey-ranks-pakistan-second-in-world/|title=Business growth: JETRO survey ranks Pakistan second in world|work=The Express Tribune}}&lt;/ref&gt;

Pakistan is one of the largest producers of natural commodities, and [[Labour force of Pakistan|its labour market]] is the 10th largest in the world. The 7-millionâ€“strong [[Pakistani diaspora]] contributed an estimated [[United States dollar|US$]]15 billion to the economy in [[Fiscal year|2014â€“15]].&lt;ref name=&quot;remit&quot; /&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.sbp.org.pk/ecodata/Homeremit.pdf|title=Pakistan &amp;#124; State Bank of Pakistan|publisher=sbp.org|accessdate=15 July 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; The major source countries of remittances to Pakistan are: the [[United Arab Emirates|UAE]]; United States; [[Saudi Arabia]]; the [[Arab states of the Persian Gulf|Gulf states]] ([[Bahrain]], [[Kuwait]], [[Qatar]], and [[Oman]]); Australia; Canada; Japan; United Kingdom; [[Norway]]; and [[Switzerland]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.dailytimes.com.pk/default.asp?page=2010\02\11\story_11-2-2010_pg5_3|title=Leading News Resource of Pakistan|publisher=Daily Times|date=11 February 2010|accessdate=29 July 2010|deadurl=yes|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/20100611043330/http://www.dailytimes.com.pk:80/default.asp?page=2010%5C02%5C11%5Cstory_11-2-2010_pg5_3|archivedate=11 June 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=&quot;young&quot;&gt;{{cite web|author=N.S. Nizami|title=Population, Labour Force and Employment|url=http://www.finance.gov.pk/survey/chapter_10/16_Population.pdf|publisher=Ministry of Finance, Pakistan|year=2010|pages=1, 2, 9, 12, 20|accessdate=18 December 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; According to the [[World Trade Organization]], Pakistan's share of overall world exports is declining; it contributed only 0.128% in 2007.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|author=Yasir kamal|title=Understanding Pakistan's Exports Flows: Results from Gravity Model Estimation|url=http://www.pitad.org.pk/indexP.php?type=completed-studies|publisher=Pakistan Instituue of Trade and Development|accessdate=30 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt; The trade deficit in the fiscal year 2010â€“11 was US$11.217 billion.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|author=Imran Ali Kundi|title=Trade deficit reaches $11.21b|url=http://www.nation.com.pk/pakistan-news-newspaper-daily-english-online/Business/10-Apr-2011/Trade-deficit-reaches-1121b|accessdate=30 December 2011|newspaper=The Nation|date=10 April 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;

==== Agriculture and Primary Sector ====
The structure of the Pakistani economy has changed from [[Agriculture in Pakistan|a mainly agricultural]] to a strong service base. Agriculture {{As of|2010|lc=y}} accounts for only 21.2% of the GDP. Even so, according to the United Nations [[Food and Agriculture Organization]], Pakistan produced 21,591,400 metric tons of wheat in 2005, more than all of Africa (20,304,585 metric tons) and nearly as much as all of South America (24,557,784 metric tons).&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.sbp.org.pk/departments/stats/PakEconomy_HandBook/Chap-1.2.pdf|title=Sectoral Share in Gross Domestic Product|year=2010|format=PDF|publisher=Federal Bureau of Statistics|page=10|accessdate=30 December 2011}}&lt;/ref&gt;  Majority of the population, directly or indirectly, is dependent on this sector. It accounts for half of employed labour force and is the largest source of foreign exchange earnings.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://www.pbs.gov.pk/content/agriculture-statistics|title=Agriculture Statistics {{!}} Pakistan Bureau of Statistics|website=www.pbs.gov.pk|access-date=2016-03-04}}&lt;/ref&gt; A large portion of the country's manufactured exports are dependent on raw materials such as cotton and hides that are part of the agriculture sector, while supply shortages and market disruptions in farm products do push up inflationary pressures. The country is also the fifth largest producer of cotton, with cotton production of 14 million bales from a modest beginning of 1.7 million bales in the early 1950s; is self sufficient in sugarcane; and is the fourth largest producer in the world of milk.  Land and water resources have not risen proportionately, but the increases have taken place mainly due to gains in labor and agriculture productivity. The major breakthrough in crop production took place in the late 1960s and 1970s due to the [[Green Revolution]] that made a significant contribution to land and yield increases of wheat and rice. Private tube wells led to a 50 percent increase in the cropping intensity which was augmented by tractor cultivation.  While the tube wells raised crop yields by 50 percent, the High Yielding Varieties (HYVs) of wheat and rice led to a 50â€“60 percent higher yield.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=iba.edu.pk/News/...drishrat/AgricultureSector_Issues_n_Prospects.docx|title=AGRICULTURE SECTOR: ISSUES AND PROSPECTS.|last=|first=|date=|website=|publisher=|access-date=4 March 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt; Meat industry accounts for 1.4 percent of overall GDP.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://www.finance.gov.pk/survey/chapter_10/03_Manufacturing.pdf|title=Manufacturing in Pakistan|last=|first=|date=|website=|publisher=Government of Pakistan|access-date=4 March 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;

==== Manufacturing ====
[[File:Tv Assembly Line 1.jpg|thumb|right|200px|A Pakistani [[television]] manufacturing factory in [[Lahore]].]]

[[Manufacturing]] is the third largest sector of the economy, accounting for 18.5 percent of Gross Domestic Product (GDP), and 13 percent of total employment. Large Scale Manufacturing (LSM), at 12.2 percent of GDP, dominates the overall sector, accounting for 66% of the sectoral share, followed by Small Scale Manufacturing, which accounts for 4.9 percent of total GDP. Pakistan's [[cement]] industry is also fast growing mainly because of demand from [[Afghanistan]] and from the domestic real estate sector. In 2013 Pakistan exported 7,708,557 [[metric tons]] of cement.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.apcma.com/data_export.html|title=All Pakistan Cement Manufacturers Association Export Data|publisher=Apcma.com|accessdate=15 October 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pakistan has an installed capacity of 44,768,250 metric tons of cement and 42,636,428 metric tons of clinker. In 2012 and 2013, the cement industry in Pakistan became the most profitable sector of the economy.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|last=Bhutta|first=Zafar|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/552042/cant-get-enough-soaring-profits-not-enough-for-cement-industry/|title=Canâ€™t get enough: Soaring profits not enough for cement industry|publisher=Tribune.com.pk|date=21 May 2013|accessdate=15 October 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

The [[Textile industry in Pakistan|textile industry]] enjoys a pivotal position in the manufacturing sector of Pakistan. Pakistan is the 8th largest exporter of textile products in Asia. This sector contributes 9.5% to the [[GDP]] and provides employment to about 15 million people or roughly 30% of the 49 million workforce of the country. Pakistan is the 4th largest producer of [[cotton]] with the third largest spinning capacity in Asia after China and India, and contributes 5% to the global spinning capacity. China is the second largest buyer of Pakistani textiles, importing US$1.527 billion of textiles last fiscal. Unlike U.S. where mostly value added textiles are imported, China buys only cotton yarn and cotton fabric from Pakistan. In 2012, Pakistani textile products accounted for 3.3% or US$1.07[[1,000,000,000|bn]] of total United Kingdom's textile imports, 12.4% or US$4.61[[1,000,000,000|bn]] of total Chinese textile imports, 2.98% or $2.98b of total United States' textile imports, 1.6% or US$0.88[[1,000,000,000|bn]] of total German textile imports and 0.7% or US$0.888[[1,000,000,000|bn]] of total Indian textile imports.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|last=Baig|first=Khurram|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/522293/anatomy-of-an-indispensable-sector-why-the-pakistan-textile-industry-cannot-die/|title=Why the Pakistan textile industry cannot die|publisher=Tribune.com.pk|date=18 March 2013|accessdate=15 October 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt;

==== Services ====
[[File:Pakistan Chrome Mines20120126 16100237 0003.jpg|thumb|right|200px|[[Surface mining]] in [[Sindh]]. Pakistan has been termed as the 'Saudi Arabia of Coal' by ''[[Forbes]]''.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.pakistantoday.com.pk/2016/03/04/city/islamabad/us-needs-to-look-at-pakistan-in-a-broader-way-not-just-through-security-prism-forbes-report/|title=US needs to look at Pakistan in a broader way, not just through security prism: Forbes report|work=pakistantoday.com.pk|accessdate=16 March 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt;]]

Services Sector has 57.7 percent share in GDP and has emerged as the main driver of economic growth.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/483436/the-unparalleled-growth-of-the-services-sector/|title=The unparalleled growth of the services sector â€“ The Express Tribune|website=The Express Tribune|language=en-US|access-date=2016-03-04}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pakistani society like other developing countries is a consumption oriented society, having a high marginal propensity to consume. The growth rate of services sector is higher than the growth rate of agriculture and industrial sector. Services sector accounts for 54 percent of GDP in 2014 and little over one-third of total employment. Services sector has strong linkages with other sectors of economy; it provides essential inputs to agriculture sector and manufacturing sector.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://www.pide.org.pk/pdf/Working%20Paper/WorkingPaper-79.pdf|title=Contribution of Services Sector in the Economy of Pakistan|last=|first=|date=|website=|publisher=|access-date=4 March 2016}}&lt;/ref&gt; Pakistan's I.T sector is regarded as among the fastest growing sector's in Pakistan. The ''[[World Economic Forum]]'', assessing the development of Information and Communication Technology in the country ranked Pakistan 111th among 144 countries in the Global Information Technology report of 2014.&lt;ref name=&quot;Farooq Baloch: WEF report&quot;&gt;{{cite news|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/374653/as-pseb-dallies-it-park-project-in-jeopardy/|title=As PSEB dallies, IT Park project in jeopardy|date=6 May 2012|newspaper=The Express Tribune|accessdate=19 May 2012|author=Farooq Baloch}}&lt;/ref&gt; {{As of|2011}}, Pakistan has over 20 million internet users and is ranked as one of the top countries that have registered a high growth rate in internet penetration.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/283253/internet-users-in-pakistan-cross-20-million-mark/|title=Internet users in Pakistan cross 20 million mark|date=28 October 2011|work=Express Tribune|accessdate=26 May 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; Overall, it has the [[List of countries by number of Internet users|27th largest population]] of internet users in the world. In the fiscal year 2012â€“2013.  The current growth rate and employment trend indicate that Pakistan's Information Communication Technology (ICT) industry will exceed the $10-billion mark by 2020.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://tribune.com.pk/story/738036/upward-move-pakistans-ict-sector-to-cross-10b-mark-says-psha/|title=Upward move: Pakistan's ICT sector to cross $10b mark, says P@SHA â€“ The Express Tribune|website=The Express Tribune|language=en-US|access-date=2016-03-04}}&lt;/ref&gt; The sector employees 12,000 and count's among top 5 freelancing nations.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite journal|date=2014-07-07|title=Pakistan Startup Report|url=http://www.slideshare.net/WorldStartupReport/pakistan-startup-report?utm_source=slideshow&amp;utm_medium=ssemail&amp;utm_campaign=weekly_digest}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://www.forbes.com/sites/danielrunde/2015/08/03/pakistan-the-next-colombia-success-story/#2720446a3b60|title=Pakistan: The Next Colombia Success Story?|website=Forbes|access-date=2016-03-04}}&lt;/ref&gt; The country has also improved its export performance in telecom, computer and information services, as the share of their exports surged from 8.2pc in 2005â€“06 to 12.6pc in 2012â€“13. This growth is much better than that of China, whose share in services exports was 3pc and 7.7pc for the same period respectively.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=http://www.dawn.com/news/1189624|title=Services sector: domestic and outward growth|last=Bhatti|first=Muhammad Umer Saleem|date=2015-06-22|website=www.dawn.com|access-date=2016-03-04}}&lt;/ref&gt;
